Jamison Brereton

30 (264)
Indra
Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra G─Бthina
22 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This long hymn follows a familiar path. It begins with three verses expressing the sacrificersтАЩ hopes that Indra will appear at their sacrifice and their worries about his continuing absence. There follow a number of verses (4тАУ14) describing the powers and deeds of Indra, past and present, including the defeats of Vr╠еtra (8) and Vala (10). This section ends with two verses (12тАУ13) on the sun and dawn, showing that Indra orders the cosmos both spatially and temporally. The riddling verse 14, with the well-known paradox of the тАЬcookedтАЭ milk contained within a тАЬrawтАЭ cow, ends this section of the hymn by seeming to identify the dawn as cow with other images of plenty for which Indra is responsible; it picks up the cow imagery already found in verse 10 concerning the release of the cows from the Vala cave. Moreover, since sacrificial gifts are distributed at the dawn ritual, the mention of dawn sets the stage for the requests for gifts at the end of the hymn.
The next part of the hymn (15тАУ17) begins abruptly with an address to Indra and a command to him: he is exhorted to come to the aid of the poet and his allies against enemies in violent battle. The final section (18тАУ21) continues the direct requests to Indra, but here for material goods to be distributed peaceably at the sac
rifice. The final verse (before the refrain) applies the model of the Vala victory to the present, beseeching Indra to continue to break open cowpens and distribute cows. As often, the concerns of the whole hymn are subtly foreshadowed in the first verse, which both establishes the sacrificers as beset by hostile forces and their sac rifice as a site for beneficial exchange with the god.
The hymn is characterized by a number of hapaxes and by affective morphology, especially in the sections devoted to IndraтАЩs opponents; the translations of some of these words are provisional.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra As noted in the published introduction, the hymn is characterized by hapaxes and very rare words, often with affective suffixes, and unusual phonology. These words include dh─Б╠Бyuс╕е (7a), gehy├а- (7b), k├║с╣З─Бru- (8b), p├нy─Бru- (8c), al─Бtс╣Ыс╣З├б- (10a), y─Бmako┼Ы├б- (15a), salal┼л╠Бka- (17c).

English translation:

тАЬThe bearers of the libations desire you; your friends pour forth the Soma; they offer copious oblations; (supported by) you they endure patiently the calumny of men, for who is so renowned as you are.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They desire you, your comrades in soma; they press the soma; they set out pleasurable offerings.
They endure the taunting of the people, for, Indra, there is no sign
from you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The desid. t├нtikс╣гante used to be assigned to тИЪtij тАШsharpenтАЩ (e.g., Wh Rts, Grassmann), but has for quite awhile been taken to тИЪtyaj тАШabandonтАЩ instead. See EWA s.v. TEJ and TYAJ, Got┼Н (1st cl., 165-66 n. 268), and in some detail Heenen (Desid. 59-60 and 147-48). Curiously Witzel Got┼Н render it as (if) an intensive to тИЪtij: тАЬSie sch├дrfen (sich) immer wieder (gegen) тАж,тАЭ despite Got┼НтАЩs own published views to the contrary. (In the Witzel Got┼Н tr., acdg. to the title pg., Maс╣Зс╕Нala III is WitzelтАЩs responsibility, however, which may account for the discrepancy.) The desiderative stem has the idiomatic sense тАШendure, supportтАЩ, and the semantic channel from (putatively) тАШdesire to abandonтАЩ to this idiom is not entirely clear. I am not convinced by the suggestions of either Got┼Н or Heenen (59-60). Instead, I think the middle voice is the key: if we assume a reflexive тАШabandon oneself toтАЩ, тАШgive oneself over toтАЩ, it is not difficult to imagine this development.

The sense of the final p─Бda depends on the meaning of praket├бс╕е, and like many derivatives of тИЪcit this word is slippery. In my view, it means both тАШsignтАЩ and тАШinsightтАЩ (that is, it reflects both the тАШappearтАЩ and тАШperceiveтАЩ values of тИЪcit). In this particular passage I take it in the former value; the point is that Indra is showing no sign of his presence or imminent arrival, and so we are subject to abuse from our rivals. For a similar usage cf. II.17.7, where the poet beseeches Indra for good fortune, and then demands kс╣Ыdh├н praket├бm тАЬmake a visible sign,тАЭ further asking for him to bring the good fortune here. In X.104.6 Indra is himself called the adhvar├бsya praket├бс╕е тАЬthe visible sign of the ceremony.тАЭ Geldner interpr. the word as Losung (тАШmotto, watchword, passwordтАЩ), which is, I suppose, possible, but I donтАЩt understand what it would mean here; Renou as тАЬle signe-pr├й(monitoire),тАЭ which is somewhat opaque to me, but seems closer to my interpr than GeldnerтАЩs; Oldenberg as тАЬHelleтАЭ (light, brightness). Witzel Got┼Н take it as an agent noun: тАЬWahrnehmer.тАЭ

Griffith

THE friends who offer Soma long to find thee: they pour forth Soma and present their viands.
They bear unmoved the cursing of the people, for all our wisdom comes from thee, O Indra.

English translation:

тАЬMaster of tawny steeds, the remotest regions are not remote for you; then come quickly with your horses; to you the steady showerer (of benefits), these sacrifices are presented; the stones (for bruising the Soma) are ready, as the fire is being kindled.тАЭ

It is for (you), the sturdy bull, that these pressings here were made and the pressing stones yoked when the fire was being kindled. с│У

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬShowerer (of benefits), who are Indra, the wearer of the helmet, the professor of opulence, the conveyor (of men beyond the evil), the leader of the numerous troops (of the Maruts), the achiever of many great deeds, the devastation of hostile (regions), the terror of your foes, where are those heroic deeds (which you have performed) against the mortal (asuras) when opposed (by them in battle).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The wearer of the helmet: su’sipra = having a handsome nose, or chin (Nirukta 6.17); now a new meaning is given: ┼Ыiras str─Бс╣Зam = a guard of the head, a helmet; the conveyor of men beyond evil: tarutra = he by whom the gods surpass or defeat the asuras

that which you, powerful one, established among mortals, even when hard-pressed, where are these manly powers of yours now, bull?

Jamison Brereton Notes

The 2nd member of tuvik┼лrm├н-, an epithet of Indra, is generally now derived from the seс╣н root тИЪcari , a derivation already found in AiG I.24, 141, 152 – hence my тАШpowerfully rangingтАЩ. See EWA s.v. tuvik┼лrm├н-. The older deriv. from тИЪkс╣Ы (e.g., Grassmann, Wh Rts; explicitly rejected by AiG II.2.776) is nonetheless still reflected in the standard tr.: Geldner тАЬder Tatenreiche,тАЭ Renou (with hesitation) тАЬaux actes (?) puissants,тАЭ Witzel Got┼Н тАЬder m├дchtig WirkendeтАЭ – even though AiG I (1896) predates all of them by a good margin, well over a century in the case of Witzel Got┼Н! There is number incongruence between the neut. sg. y├бd of the rel. clause and neut. pl. ty─Б╠БтАж v─лry─Б╠Ас╣Зi. The y├бd is, as it were, an anticipatory collective: тАЬwhat(ever) you did тАж where are those deeds?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The next two vss. develop the theme sounded in p─Бda d of vs. 1.: IndraтАЩs absence. In vs. 2 we point out that for Indra nothing is very far away, so he could, and should, easily come here, where the sacrifice is invitingly set out for him. In vs. 3 we provide a flattering description of IndraтАЩs great powers and then plaintively ask where these powers are now.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou alone casting down the firmly-footed (asuras) proceed, destroying the Vс╣Ыtras, and obedient to your command the heaven and earth and the mountains stood as if immoveable.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For you, stirring the unstirrable, alone range about smashing obstacle after obstacle.

It is following your commandment that heaven and earth and the mountains stand like (pillars) implanted.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As has often been pointed out, the redupl. pres. to тИЪhan, j├нghnate, almost always takes plural objects, and so, at least in this formation, reduplication seems correlated with repetitive action. This semantic nuance is strengthened here by the syntactic construction, with the redupl. pres. in the participle (j├нghnam─Бnaс╕е) construed with a quasi-auxiliary c├бrasi. (Cf. 14b below.) Although c├бrasi does have lexical meaning (тАШyou range/roam/wanderтАЩ), the lexical value is weak enough here that the verb can seem to be a marker of the progressive present: тАЬyou go about / keep / are (constantly) smashing.тАЭ On the other hand, it is possible that тИЪcar in its lexical value may be resonating with tuvik┼лrm├н- тАШpowerfully rangingтАЩ in 3b (see comm. there). However, it is hard to know whether that root connection would still be perceived by the contemporary audience – it certainly has escaped most of the modern audience – given the phonological distance between the two words and the fact that tuvik┼лrm├н- is simply an epithet of Indra and its own lexical value may have become attenuated.

There is a faint phonological echo between vс╣Ыtr─Б╠Бin b and vrat─Б╠Б(ya) in d, which occupy the same metrical position.

Griffith

For, overthrowing what hath ne’er been shaken, thou goest forth alone destroying Vrtras.
For him who followeth thy Law the mountains and heaven and earth stand as if firmly stablished.

Geldner

Denn du f├╝rwahr, der du das Unersch├╝tterliche ersch├╝tterst, ziehst alleine aus, die Feinde erschlagend. Auf dein Gebot standen Himmel und Erde, die Berge wie festgerammt.

Grassmann

Denn du f├╝rwahr bewegst das unbewegte, ziehst aus allein, zu t├╢dten deine Feinde; Sich f├╝gend deinem Willen stehn die Berge, wie festgebannt der Himmel und die Erde.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou alone, when invoked by many, and the slayer of Vс╣Ыtra, by your prowess, did say firmly (to the gods), fear not! Indra, endowed with opulence, vast is your grasp, wherewith you have seized these unbounded regions, heaven and earth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And, o you who are much invoked with acclamations, in fearlessness you alone talked tough, since you are the obstacle-smasher.
Even these two world-halves without limitsтАФwhen you grabbed them together, bounteous Indra, it was just a handful for you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I am not certain how to construe ┼Ыr├бvobhiс╕е. The published translation takes it with the voc. puruh┼лta: тАЬmuch invoked with acclamations.тАЭ But I am not entirely happy about construing a full noun with a voc. that ordinarily stands alone (as in, e.g., 7d, 8a). Geldner tr. тАЬr├╝hmlich,тАЭ which seems designed to be as untethered to the sentence as possible.

Renou takes it with the speaking of p─Бda b: тАЬтАж seul avec tes remons tu as parl├й (un langage) ferme,тАЭ but I donтАЩt understand what that means; Witzel Got┼Н like Renou, except tr. тАЬmit Ruhmes(taten),тАЭ which again I donтАЩt follow.

I have given the idiom dс╣Ыс╕╖h├бm тИЪvad a mildly slangy turn (similarly in X.48.6); the collocation of a verb of speaking and an adverb referring to a physical quality seems to invite it. тАЬSpeak firmlyтАЭ would be a more neutral rendering than тАЬtalk tough,тАЭ but p─Бda d, which describes heaven and earth as a mere тАЬhandfulтАЭ for Indra, also seems to belong to a vivid and informal register.

The participial phrase vс╣Ыtrah─Б╠Бs├бn contains, unusually, a non-concessive nominative of the pres. part. of тИЪas тАШbeтАЩ. It seems here to be definitional and to pick up and summarize 4b ├йko vс╣Ыtr─Б╠Бc├бrasi j├нghnam─Бnaс╕е тАЬyou alone range about [/keep] smashing obstacles.тАЭ As discussed immed. above, the redupl. pres. part. combined with a quasi-auxiliary depicts this as repetitive, indeed habitual, action – and the ├йkaс╕е indicates that only Indra engages in it. Our phrase here, vс╣Ыtrah─Б╠Бs├бn, comes to the appropriate conclusion: since you and you alone keep smashing obstacles, you are The Obstacle-Smasher, par excellence.

Griffith

E’en these two boundless worlds to thee, O Indra, what time thou graspest them, are but a handful.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet (your car), Indra, drawn by your horses (rush) downwards (upon the asuras); let your destroying thunder-bolt fall upon your enemies; slay those that assail in front or in rear, or that fly (from the combat); make the universe (the abode of) truth; (let such power) be concentrated in you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Come) forth along an easy slope with your two fallow bays; let your mace come forth, pulverizing the rivals.
Smash those facing you, those following, those turned away. Make all this come true; let it be accomplished.

Jamison Brereton Notes

S─Бyaс╣Зa. supplies тАШchariotтАЩ as the subj. of p─Бda a, and in this he is followed by the standard tr. as well as Oldenberg Although this is perfectly harmless and certainly possible, I do not understand why supplying a subject not found in the context is desirable, much less necessary. I admit that it would allow us to use the etu of pr├б тАж etu in b as the gapped verb with the pr├б of a, but Rigvedic poetic syntax is flexible enough to allow a 2nd ps. substitution in such a gapped phrase (pr├б тАж *ihi, anticipating pr├б тАж etu). The fact that 2b has a similar phrase with Indra as the 2nd sg.

supplied subject – ─Б╠Бt├║ pr├б y─Бhi тАж h├бribhy─Бm – also supports my assumption that the default subject is Indra.

Unfortunately the voc. indra in 6a was omitted in the published translation The p─Бda should read тАЬ(Come) forth along an easy slope with your two fallow bays, o Indra.тАЭ

Griffith

Forthwith thy Bay steeds down the steep, O Indra, forth, crushing foemen, go thy bolt of thunder!
Slay those who meet thee, those who flee, who follow: make all thy promise true; be all completed.

Geldner

Dein Wagen soll fein mit dem Falbenpaar in gestrecktem Laufe, deine Keule soll die Feinde zermalmend vordringen, o Indra. Erschlage sie, wenn sie sich entgegenstellen, wenn sie von hinten kommen, wenn sie den R├╝cken kehren ! Mach alles wahr; es soll ein Ende gemacht werden!

Grassmann

Vor eil’ dein Wagen j├дhlings mit den F├╝chsen, und vor dein Blitz, die Feinde niederschmetternd, Erschlag’ die vordern, mittleren und letzten; lass alles wahr sein und von dir vollendet.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe man to whom you grant, lord of power, (your good-will), enjoys unprecedented domestic (prosperity); Indra, who are invoked by many, your auspicous favour, which is obtained by oblations, is the giver of unbounded wealth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Which is obtained by oblation: sumatirghс╣Ыt─Бc─л = that which goes to or obtains clarified butter, havir a├▒cati, pr─Бpnoti

Jamison Brereton

To whatever mortal you have provided sustenance, he takes a portion of the household goods, even what is not yet apportioned.
Auspicious is your benevolence and covered with ghee, much-invoked Indra; your generosity provides a thousand gifts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

dh─Б╠Бyuс╕е is a hapax. The stem is generally listed as dh─Б╠Бyu- (so Grassmann) and would therefore have to be a masc. nom. sg. here, but the standard tr. render it as obj. of ├бdadh─Бс╕е. This interpr. requires it to be a neut. -us-stem, which is easily possible (see, e.g., Oldenberg). Oldenberg suggests that it belongs to тИЪdh─Б and that dh─Б╠Бyur ├бdadh─Бс╕е is an etymological figure like ├бbhaktam тАж bhajate in b. I prefer the analysis suggested in AiG II.2.470 linking it to тИЪdh─Б(y) тАШsuckle, nourishтАЩ, thus a neut. -us-stem exactly parallel to neut. dh─Б╠Бyas- тАШnourishmentтАЩ. This analysis seems to be reflected in RenouтАЩs тАЬtu as accord├й la satisfaction-nourrici├иre,тАЭ though RenouтАЩs (in)famous hyphenated portmanteaus are capacious enough to include many possibilities.

I am not entirely sure what p─Бda b is about: is this a legal issue, having to do with what is held in common? or with what hasn’t (yet) been divided by inheritance? Or is it simply that nobody has distributed the goods yet? X.112.10d, adduced by Geldner, is similar: ├бbhakte cid ─Б╠Бbhaj─Б r─Бy├й asm─Б╠Бn, but that p─Бda follows one in which Indra is urged to do battle and so the most likely interpr. there is that we are asking for a share in the as-yet-undivided spoils of war. Here, however, the goods are specifically identified as gehy├а- тАШbelonging to the householdтАЩ. This is the only occurrence of this stem in the RV; it is found in AVP (VI.14.8, VII. 11.3; see Arlo Griffiths ed. and tr.) and later, and geh├б- тАШhouseтАЩ, from which it is derived, first occurs in VS. The etymology of geh├б- is quite unclear (cf. EWA s.v.), as is its relationship to synonymous gс╣Ыh├б-. The former is quite widespread in MIA, beginning already in A┼Ыoka, but it cannot be simply a Middle Indic form of gс╣Ыh├б- at least acdg. to the standard sound laws (pace older accounts such as AiG I.39), though it is quite possible that it has guс╣Зa in an adj. derived from MIA gihi(n) тАШhouseholderтАЩ (тЖР*gс╣Ыhin- ), (a-)giha-. In any event it seems likely that the word was imported into Vedic from MIA and that the use of this unusual stem here signals a particular social or legal institution for which we have no other evidence.

Griffith

The man to whom thou givest as Provider enjoys domestic plenty undivided.
Blest, Indra, is thy favour dropping fatness: thy worship, Much-invoked! brings gifts in thousands.

Geldner

Welchem Sterblichen du Gen├╝ge getan hast, der hat Anteil an dem noch unverteilten Hauswesen. Gl├╝ckbringend ist deine Gnade, o Indra, in Schmalz gehend; tausendschenkend deine Freigebigkeit, du Vielgerufener.

Grassmann

der Sterbliche, dem gabenreich du schenktest erlangt, o Indra, nicht erlangten Hausrath, Fetttriefend ist und heilvoll deine G├╝te und tausendfach die Gab’, o vielgerufner.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, who is invoked by many, grind to dust the reviling malevolent Vс╣Ыtra opposing you, dwelling with the mother of the D─Бnavas, and increasing in might, until having deprived him of hand and foot, you have destroyed him by your strength.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 18.69; having deprived him of hand: sahad─Бnum kс╣гiyantam sampiс╣Зak kuс╣З─Бrum: the allegory is the destruction of the cloud; or, it may mean, united with the d─Бnavas;

Sahau = sahas, strength;

Kс╣гiyantam = badham─Бnam, rain opposing; or, nikaс╣нavartam─Бnam, being near to;

Kuс╣З─Бru = either a proper name of an asura, a noisy one, kvaс╣Зana┼Ы─лlam, or evil speaking, durvacavadanam; or, parikavaс╣Зana, loud-sounding; anothe rinterpretation: crush the increasing cloud shedding water, sahad─Бnum udakad─Бnapetam; abiding in the sky, kс╣гiyantam ─Бk─Б┼Ыe nivasantam; and thundering, kuс╣З─Бrum = garjantam

Jamison Brereton

The one dwelling together with (his mother) D─Бnu, the handless vermin did you utterly crush, much-invoked Indra.
With your powerful (mace), Indra, you smashed at the sneering footless Vr╠еtra, who was growing strong.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. contains two difficult words, k├║с╣З─Бru- (b) and p├нy─Бru- (c). It is surely no accident that they appear p─Бda-final in successive p─Бdas and are rhyme forms. The former is a hapax (though the vs. is repeated in the VS [M─Б XVIII.69, K─Б XX.5.2]). It has been glossed тАШlame in the armтАЩ on the basis of a supposed connection with Ep, Cl kuс╣Зi- тАШid.тАЩ (cf., e.g., AiG II.2.288, KEWA s.v. kuс╣Зiс╕е, EWA s.v. kuс╣З─Бru-). But the chronological and morphological distance between the two words speaks against this connection, as does the fact that kuс╣Зi- is likely a Dravidian borrowing (see KEWA).

Moreover, since Vс╣Ыtra is a snake and is specifically called тАШhandlessтАЩ here, it is unlikely that he would have an arm to be lame in. Wiser heads generally take it as a PN (so the standard tr., as well as Mayrhofer PN [though with ?]). However, this cautious course is not very satisfactory either. The enemy is most definitely Vс╣Ыtra: his name appears in c, his motherтАЩs (D─Бnu) in a. Why would he be called by a different name, esp. one that never appears elsewhere? Unfortunately I do not have a strong alternative. However, I would point to k├║с╣Зapa-, which means something like тАШcarrion, corpseтАЩ (AV┼Ъ XI.9.10, 10.10.4, 8; MS IV.9.19; тЙЕ kuс╣Зap├б- TS XI.2.10.2, where human and equine kuс╣Зap├б-s are distinguished) on which various nasty critters are invited to feed, and to various later forms of (-t)kuс╣Зa- referring to various bugs (cf. Kuiper [Aryans passim], Turner [CDIAL s.vv. k├║с╣Зapa-, kuс╣Зa-], and P─Бli mankuna-). On the basis of these shaky parallels I suggest that k├║с╣З─Бru- means something like тАШverminтАЩ or perhaps even тАШcorpseтАЩ. It owes its pejorative -─Бru-suffix to p├нy─Бru-; cf. also ┼Ыar─Б╠Бru- in X.86.9, which I tr. тАШnoxious creatureтАЩ. Of course, ku- is a common pejorative prefix as well. Perhaps the word is simply constructed of pejorative affixes with a hiatus-breaking с╣З! Or – a better possibility – it may represent *ku-nara-─Бru- тАШill-manlyтАЩ, with haplology and MIA retroflexion of the nasal. My point here is not to claim any of these suggestions as definitive, but to show that this completely opaque word resonates with other words in several different directions and therefore assuming a lexical meaning rather than taking it as a PN is the better course. However, in the published translation тАШverminтАЩ should be followed by a question mark.

The 2nd difficult word, p├нy─Бru-, is by comparison much simpler. It must be derived from тИЪp─л тАШsneer, tauntтАЩ, whose pres. p─л╠Бyati is attested 3x already in the RV. It contains the same pejorative -─Бru-suffix as k├║с╣З─Бru-, ┼Ыar─Б╠Бru- – though it should be noted that not all -─Бru-suffixed words are pejorative: vand─Б╠Бru- is quite positive, and the mysterious hapax j├бb─Бru- (IV.5.7) is at worst neutral but probably positive.

Griffith

Thou, Indra, Much-invoked! didst crush to pieces Kunaru handless fiend who dwelt with Danu.
Thou with might, Indra, smotest dead the scorner, the footless Vrtra as he waxed in vigour.

Der da lag sammt dem D├дmon, vielgerufner, den trafst du, Indra, handlos ward er, armlahm; Den b├╢sen Vritra, ihn der m├дchtig anwuchs, zerschlugst mit Kraft du, Indra, fusslos ward er.

English translation:

тАЬYou have fixed tranquil in its position the vast unbounded and wandering earth; the showerer (of benefits) has upheld the heaven and the firmament; let the waters engendered by you here descend.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You set down in its seat the whole, great, limitless, vital earth, Indra. The bull propped up heaven and the midspace. Let the waters flow here, propelled by you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The pf. of тИЪsad is generally intrans.(/reflex.) тАШsat (oneself) downтАЩ, but in several instances must be trans. тАШset downтАЩ, as it is here. See K├╝mmel 542-43.

There is no agreement on the meaning of the adj. s─Бman├б-, found in the RV only here and in the wedding hymn (X.85.11). Grassmann тАШgemeinschaftlichтАЩ (fld. by Witzel Got┼Н), Geldner тАШg├╝tige (?)тАЩ, Renou тАШabondanteтАЩ (but in EVP XVI, ad X.85.11, he suggests that in our passage it means тАШattel├йe-avecтАЩ with which тАШheavenтАЩ should be supplied), AiG II.2.136 тАШreichтАЩ. I suggest that itтАЩs a vс╣Ыddhi deriv. of s├бmana- тАШgatheringтАЩ, meaning тАШrelated to the gathering/aggregateтАЩ, hence тАШwholeтАЩ. This does not work so well in X.85.11, but there there is a pun on -s─Б╠Бman- тАШtuneтАЩ, and the word seems simply to mean тАШtogetherтАЩ vel sim.

Griffith

Thou hast established in her seat, O Indra, the level earth, vast, vigorous, unbounded.
The Bull hath propped the heaven and air’s mid-region. By thee sent onward let the floods flow hither.

Geldner

Du, Indra, hast die g├╝tige, eifrige, gro├Яe, unbegrenzte Erde an ihren Platz gesetzt. Er st├╝tzte den Himmel, der Bulle, den Luftraum; auf dein Gehei├Я sollen hier die Gew├дsser flie├Яen.

Grassmann

Du setztest Indra hin die gleiche Erde an ihren Sitz, die saft’ge, reiche, weite; Es festigte der Stier die Luft, den Himmel, von dir erregt hier m├╢gen Fluten rinnen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe heavy cloud, the receptacle of water, dreading you its destroyer, opened out before (you had cast your bolt); then Indra made easily-traversed paths for the waters to issue, and desirable and loud sounding they proceeded to the (waters of the earth) invoked of many.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Heavy cloud: al─Бtс╣Ыс╣Зo valaс╕е = a cloud, that which by its abundance of water, is able to do mischief; cf. Nirukta 6.2; desirable and loud-sounding: pr─Бvan puruh┼лtam, v─Бс╣Зirdhamant─лс╕е = vanan─лyaс╕е ‘sabd─Бyam─Бn─Бs-t─Б ─Бpaс╕е puruh┼лtam bahubhir─Бh┼лtam p─Бrthivam udakam abhyagacchan;

Dhamant─лс╕е = dhamatirgatikarm─Б (Nirukta 6.2)

Jamison Brereton

Vala, the enclosure of cattle, unquiet and fearful, opened up (even) before being struck, o Indra.
He [=Indra] made the paths easy to travel, to drive out the cows. The choir (of Aс╣Еgirases) aided the much-invoked one, blowing (on their instruments).

Jamison Brereton Notes

On al─Бtс╣Ыс╣З├б- see comm. ad I.166.7. In this passage though тАШunquietтАЩ does not seem a normal feature of Vala, it can be applied proleptically, characterizing its opening up in fear of IndraтАЩs blow.

Note the phonetic figure in ab: al─Б.. vala тАж vrajo … vy ─Бra, with -tс╣Ыс╣З- тАж - ndr- nestled in the 1st p─Бda; the d p─Бda also has phonetic rep.: pr─Бvan v─Бniс╕е.

The standard tr. all supply the Maruts with v─Б╠Бс╣З─лс╕е тАШchoirтАЩ. But as Schmidt (Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra 141) points out, the Maruts do not ordinarily participate in the Vala myth; it is the Aс╣Еgirases who are IndraтАЩs back-up band. See III.31.4ff.

Griffith

He who withheld the kine, in silence I yielded in fear before thy blow, O Indra.
He made paths easy to drive forth the cattle. Loud-breathing praises helped the Much-invoked One.

Geldner

Ohne zur├╝ckzufordern hat sich Vala, der Rinderpferch, noch vor deinem Schlage furchtsam aufgetan. Er machte die Wege frei, um die Rinder herauszutreiben. Die blasenden Ch├╢re der Marut ermutigten dich, den Vielgerufenen.

Grassmann

Der geiz’ge Vala und der Stall der K├╝he, sie gaben nach aus Furcht vor deinem Hiebe; Die Pfade bahnt’ er, trieb heraus die K├╝he, der Winde Ton war lieb dem vielgerufnen.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ ! рдЕрд▓рд╛рддреГрдгреЛ рдмрд▓реЛ рдмреНрд░рдЬреЛ рднрдпрдорд╛рдиреЛ рднрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕реБрдЧрд╛рдиреНрдкрдереЛ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рд░ рдпрдГ рдкреБрд░рд╛ рдЧреЛрд░реНрд╣рдиреНрддреЛрд░рдХреГрдгреЛрджреНрдпрд╛ рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрддрдВ рдзрдордиреНрддреАрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгреАрд░реНрдЧрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рддрд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рдирд┐рд░рдЬреЗ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рд░ реерезрежрее

рдпреЛрд╜рдпрдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдПрдХрдГ рдЕрд╕рд╣рд╛рдп рдПрд╡ рд╕рдиреН рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрдореН рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рджреНрдпрд╛рдВ рджреНрд╡реЗ рдПрддреЗ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ рд╕рдореАрдЪреА рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рд╕рдВрдЧрддреЗ рд╡рд╕реБрдорддреА рдзрдирдпреБрдХреНрддреЗ рд╕рддреНрдпреМ рдЖ рдкрдкреНрд░реМ рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН рдкреВрд░рдпрд╛рдорд╛рд╕ ред рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рд╣реЗ рд╢реВрд░ рд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпреЛрдкреЗрдд рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд░рдереАрдГ рд░рдерд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕рдГ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╕рдореАрдХреЗ рд╕рдореАрдкреЗ рдЗрд╖рдГ рд╕реНрдерд╛рддреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреН ‘рд╕рдпреБрдЬрдГ рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╛рдиреНред рд╡рдЬрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГред рддрд╛рдирд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рддреН рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН рдЕрднрд┐ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдп ред рд░рдерд╛рд░реВрдврд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдорддреНрд╕рдореАрдкрдВ рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рдорд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫреЗрддрд┐ рднрд╛рд╡рдГ рее рд╡рд╕реБрдорддреАред ’ рд╡рд╛ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рд┐ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕рд╡рд░реНрдгрджреАрд░реНрдШрдГ ред рдкрдкреНрд░реМред’ рдкреНрд░рд╛ рдкреВрд░рдгреЗ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд▓рд┐рдЯрд┐ рдгрд▓рд┐ тАШрдЖрдд рдФ рдгрд▓рдГ’ рдЗрддреНрдпреМрдХрд╛рд░рдГ ред рдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрдГ ред рдЗрд╖рдГ ред рдЗрд╖реБ рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рдпрд╛рдореН ’ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рджрд┐рдЧреБрдкрдзрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдГ рдХрдГ ред рдХрд┐рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рджрдЧреБрдгрдГ ред рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрд╕реНрд╡рд░рдГ ред рд░рдереАрдГ ред рд░рдереЛрд╜рд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рдорддреБрдмрд░реНрдереЗ ’ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реАрд╡рдирд┐рдкреМ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдИрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ ред рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрд╕реНрд╡рд░рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra alone has filled the two,both earth and heaven mutually combined, and abounding with wealth; do you hero, mounted in your car, come with your harnessed horses from the firmament, impatient to be near us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The oneтАФIndraтАФfilled the twoтАФearth and heavenтАФthe joint repositories of goods.
And from the midspace, at their join [i.e., of heaven and earth], as charioteer of refreshment (bring) us prizes in yoke together, o
champion.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a begins with an elementary numerical figure: ├йko dv├й тАЬthe one the two,тАЭ subject and object of ─Б╠Бpaprau respectively, both of which are identified in the 2nd p─Бda. The juxtaposition of the two numbers is responsible for my tr. ├йka- as тАШthe oneтАЩ, rather than тАШaloneтАЩ as elsewhere in the hymn (vss. 4, 5).

Because of the voc. ┼Ы┼лra, at least p─Бda d (and probably also c) shows a switch to 2nd ps. from the 3rd ps. of ab. Since there are no verbs in cd, at least one needs to be supplied. Most tr. (Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н], Klein [DGRV I.442], Scarlatta [431]) take c and d as separate clauses, supplying impvs. тАЬcomeтАЭ and тАЬbringтАЭ respectively. This is possible, but I follow Renou in taking cd as a single clause – though do not follow his interpr. of iс╣г├бс╕е as a verb (тАШenvoieтАЩ, presumably to тИЪiс╣г тАШsendтАЩ).

All tr., incl. Renou, take sam─лk├й as тАЬin battleтАЭ (or, closer to the root sense in my opinion, Scarlatta тАЬTreffenтАЭ). Although this noun generally has the meaning тАШencounterтАЩ, it is a straightforward derivative of samy├бc- тАШunited, conjoinedтАЩ, and here I take it to refer to the тАЬjoinтАЭ of Heaven and Earth, which would define the midspace. Note that p─Бda-final sam─лk├й matches p─Бda-final du. sam─лc─л╠Бin a, referring to Heaven and Earth.

I supply тАШbringтАЩ as the verb of cd, with say├║jaс╕е тАж v─Б╠Бj─Бn as obj. There are several possible interpr of iс╣г├бс╕е. As just noted, Renou takes it as a verb. Assuming (with everyone else) that it belongs to the root noun ├нс╣г-, there are two possible analyses, as gen. (/abl.) sg. or nom./acc. pl., although in the latter case we would prefer it to be accented ├нс╣гaс╕е (cf. the acc. pl. ├нс╣гaс╕е in 18b). Both Klein and Scarlatta take it as acc. pl.; I agree with Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) in construing it as gen. sg. with rath─л╠Бс╕е.

English translation:

тАЬS┼лrya harms not the quarters (of the horizon), set open daily (for his journey), the progeny of Harya┼Ыva; when he has traversed the roads (he is to travel), then he lets loose his horses, for such is his office.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Harms not the quarters: di┼Ыaс╕е s┼лryo na min─Бti na hiс╣Гsati = he does not injure;

Harya┼Ыva = Indra, or he with the tawny horses

Jamison Brereton

The Sun does not confound the directions as they are directed, as they are day after day propelled forth by him of the fallow bays.
When he has fully reached (the end) of the road, only after that does he perform his unyoking of the horses. But that is his (way).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The grammar of ab is so straightforward that it is easy to overlook how odd the statement is. It is not surprising that the sun does not confound the quarters or directions (d├н┼Ыaс╕е); after all, the layout of the cosmos is not likely to be altered by the sun as it passes through. But what does it mean that these same d├н┼Ыaс╕е are pras┼лt─Б╠Бс╕е every day by Indra? The ppl. can only belong either to тИЪs┼л тАШpropelтАЩ or тИЪs┼л тАШgive birthтАЩ, far more likely the former (pace Witzel Got┼Н, who seem to take it to the latter): only the former is found with pr├б and in fact 9d contains an exactly parallel expression, tv├бy─Б тАж pr├бs┼лt─Бс╕е тАЬpropelled by you.тАЭ Geldner tr. тАЬvom Falbenlenker bestimmten,тАЭ but тАШdetermined, fixed, setтАЩ seems the exactly opposite of what pr├б тИЪs┼л ordinarily means, including in nearby 9d. Such a meaning makes more sense of this vs. but at the expense of arbitrarily assigning a unique meaning to this rather common lexeme. If we take the idiom seriously, the hemistich seems to be saying that while the sun respects the placement of the parts of the cosmos, Indra pushes them around in some fashion, remaking or reconfiguring the cosmos daily. I simply do not understand this; I must be missing something. Perhaps Indra arranges the d├н┼Ыaс╕е every day in a slightly new way for the sunтАЩs road? The sun is presumably the subj. of ─Б╠Бnaс╣н; so the standard tr.

The cmpd h├бrya┼Ыvapras┼лta- technically has three members – that is a 2nd member ppl. (pr├бs┼лta-) whose 1st member is itself a cmpd. This would be somewhat unusual for the RV, where cmpd size is quite limited. But the bv. h├бry-a┼Ыva- is so frozen as an epithet of Indra that it was probably not fully perceived as a cmpd. Cf. the exactly equivalent ├нndra-pras┼лta- (1x). Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) seems to interpr. ├бdhvanaс╕е as acc. pl. (тАЬWenn sie ihre Wege vollendet hatтАЭ). Because I am not at all certain that тИЪna┼Ы can be used that way with an acc., I take ├бdhvanaс╕е as gen. sg., with a supplied тАШendтАЩ; cf. V.54.10 ├бdhvanaс╕е p─Бr├бm a┼Ыnutha with the same root. So apparently also Renou

├б┼Ыvaiс╕е is an instr. of separation with vim├│canam.

Griffith

Surya transgresses not the ordered limits set daily by the Lord of Tawny Coursers.
When to the goal he comes, his journey ended, his Steeds he looses: this is Indra’s doing.

Geldner

Die Sonne verfehlt nicht die vorgezeichneten Richtungen, die Tag f├╝r Tag vom Falbenlenker bestimmten. Wenn sie ihre Wege vollendet hat, dann macht sie mit den Rossen Ausspann. Das aber ist sein Werk.

Grassmann

Die Sonne ├дndert nicht die festen Ziele, der Tag f├╝r Tag vom Rosseherrn gesetzt sind, Wenn sie die Bahn durchlaufen, dann erst lenkt sie zur Einkehr mit den Rossen, das ist sein Werk.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAl,l me are anxious to behold the great and variegated host (of the solar rays) at the issuing of the dawn after the night has been displaced; and when the morning has come, they recognize the many great and glorious acts of Indra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They desire to see, at the coming of Dawn from night, the great glittering face of her who shines forth [=Dawn].
They all know when she has come with her greatness. Many are the well-done deeds of Indra.

Griffith

Men gladly in the course of night would look on the broad bright front of the refulgent Morning;
And all acknowledge, when she comes in glory, the manifold and goodly works of Indra.

Geldner

English translation:

тАЬA great light has been shed upon the rivers; the cow yet immature grazes, charged with the ripe (milk), for Indra has plural ced in the cow all this collected sweetness for food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Great light was deposited in her udder. Herself raw, the cow roams about carrying the cooked (milk).
Every sweetness was brought together in the ruddy one, when Indra established her for nourishment.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On vakс╣г├бс╣З─Б- тАШbellyтАЩ (here tr. тАШudderтАЩ perhaps misleadingly) as a pl. tantum, see comm. ad X.27.16.

carati b├нbhrat─л is another instance of quasi-auxiliary тИЪcar + pres. part. (also to a redupl. pres.); cf. 4b. Here, carati seems to have more lexical value than in vs. 4.

Griffith

A mighty splendour rests upon her bosom: bearing ripe milk the Cow, unripe, advances.
All sweetness is collected in the Heifer, sweetness which Indra made for our enjoyment.

Geldner

Ein gro├Яes Licht ist in ihren Eutern verwahrt: die rohe Kuh wandelt die gekochte Milch tragend. Aller Wohlgeschmack ward in der Kuh vereinigt, als Indra sie zur Nahrung bestimmte.

Grassmann

Ein grosser Glanz ist in den Leib gesetzet, die rohe Kuh geht tragend garen Milchtrank Vereint ist alles S├╝sse in der Milchkuh, was Indra machte zum Genuss der Menschen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, be firm, for there are obstructors of your path; secure to the worshipper and his friends (the means of completing) the sacrifice; mortal enemies bearing bows, armed with mischievous weapons, and coming with evil intent, must be destroyed (by you).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mortal enemies: marty─Бsaс╕е = m─Бrayit─Бraс╕е, killers, murderers

Jamison Brereton

Indra, stand fast! The (enemiesтАЩ) тАЬjourney-bucketsтАЭ [=chariots] have come. Do your best for the sacrifice, for the singer, for your
comrades.
The mortals who use dirty tricks, those of evil ways, the cheaters
wearing quivers are to be smashed.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The sense of the hapax y─Бmako┼Ы├б- is unclear. Geldner takes it as traveling trunks: тАЬDie Reisetruhen sind bereitтАЭ; sim. Oldenberg But the image of Indra standing by overseeing the loading of his luggage verges on the absurd. Oldenberg suggests rather that it is we who have come with empty suitcases, hoping Indra will fill them. Renou takes y─Бma- to тИЪy─Б тАШbeseechтАЩ rather than тИЪy─Б тАШdrive, travelтАЩ, yielding тАЬles vases de la pri├иre.тАЭ Since there is no comm. in EVP XVII, we will never know what he meant by that; it is certainly not transparent. My tr. тАЬjourney-bucketтАЭ is meant as a slangy term for chariot (тАШbucketтАЩ can be so used in English for an old or badly maintained car); certainly the use of k├│┼Ыa- тАШbucket, caskтАЩ to refer to (a part of) a chariot is clear from VIII.20.8, 22.9. Witzel Got┼НтАЩs тАЬWagenk├╢rbeтАЭ is similar.

I also think that the chariots in question belong to the enemies mentioned in cd; this might account for the slangy designation of their vehicles – rather like referring to a rivalтАЩs car as a jalopy. In any case it would seem odd to command Indra to stand fast and them immediately get on a chariot and go traveling.

Griffith

Barring the way they come. Be firm, O Indra; aid friends to sacrifice and him who singeth.
These must be slain by thee, malignant mortals, armed with ill arts, our quiverbearing foemen.

Indra, bleib fest ! Die Reisetruhen sind bereit. Tu dem S├дnger und seinen Freunden f├╝r das Opfer zu Dank! Die hinterlistigen Sterblichen, deren Trachten b├╢se ist, die Schelme, die den K├╢cher umhaben, sollen erschlagen werden!

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe sound (of your bolt) has been heard by the approaching foes; hurl upon them the consuming thunder-bolt, cut them up by the root, oppose; Maghavan, overcome, slay the r─Бkс╣гasas, complete (the sacrifice).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

All around your battle-cry is heard by the closest foes. Smash your most scorching missile down on them.
Cleave them below; break them apart; overwhelm them. Smash the
demonic force, bounteous one; make them subject to you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. all take the gh├│с╣гa- to be emanating from the foes, but the instr. am├нtraiс╕е with ┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Зve should make it an agent of the hearing (тАЬis heard by тАжтАЭ) not a source of the sound. GeldnerтАЩs (/Witzel Got┼НтАЩs) тАЬvonтАЭ and RenouтАЩs supplied тАЬ(faite) dтАЩennemisтАЭ show their need to overrule the syntax. I see no reason why it should not be IndraтАЩs battle-cry, striking fear in all who hear it.

Griffith

A cry is beard from enemies most near us: against them send thy fiercest-flaming weapon.
Rend them from under, crush them and subdue them. Slay, Maghavan, and make the fiends our booty.

Geldner

Man h├╢rt das Geschrei von den ganz nahen Feinden. Schleudere auf sie deinen gl├╝henden Keil! Hau ihn unten ab, zerspalte, bezwinge ihn, erschlage den Dunkelgeist, du Gabenreicher, bring ihn in deine Gewalt!

Grassmann

Der L├дrm erschallt von allern├дchsten Feinden, auf sie wirf nieder deinen sch├дrfsten Blitzstrahl; Zerbrich, zerspalte sie von unten, siege, den Nachtgeist schlag’, o starker, unterwirf ihn.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬplural ck the r─Бkс╣гasas, Indra, by the root; cut as under the middle, blight the summit; to whatever remote (regions) you have driven the sinner, cast upon the enemy of the Veda your consuming weapon.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The enemy of the Veda: brahmadviс╣гe = brahmaс╣Зadveс╣гak─Бriс╣Зe, or him who entertains hatred against the Brahman; but, brahma may mean the prayer of the Vedas, or the Vedas, or perhaps, the religion or ritual of the followers of the Veda

Jamison Brereton

Tear out the demonic power, root and all, Indra; cleave its middle; shatter its top.
How far have you sent it scooting? Hurl your scorching lance at the hater of the sacred formulation.

Jamison Brereton Notes

salal┼л╠Бka- is yet another peculiar word that brings our interpr. to a standstill.

The current standard interpr. is тАЬindulgence, patienceтАЭ vel sim. (Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н] тАЬNachsichtтАЭ). I do not understand where such a meaning would come from.

Mayrhofer (KEWA s.v.) suggests тИЪsс╣Ы in the meaning тАШsich erstreckenтАЩ, but the semantic channel from one to the other seems blocked to me. Although a deriv. from тИЪsс╣Ы seems likely, a more literal sense of that root, тАШrun, flowтАЩ, provides better sense.

(The older interpr. of the word was тАШzerflossenтАЩ or тАШumherschweifendтАЩ [Grassmann, etc.].) Both the lтАЩs and the affective -┼л╠Бka-suffix suggest a slangy or low-register word – hence my тАЬsend scooting.тАЭ Grassmann suggests a preform *salsal┼л╠Бka-, presumably because - ┼л╠Бka- is often added to intensively reduplicated stems (see AiG II.2.498)(cf. j─Бgar┼л╠БkaIII.54.7). This seems possible (though not, of course, necessary), and тАЬsend scootingтАЭ is also meant to reflect an intensive/iterative sense. Note that salal┼л╠Бkam phonologically resembles sah├бm┼лlam in p─Бda a (in almost the same metrical position), which may help account for the presence of salal┼л╠Бkam in the vs. and could also have facilitated a dissimilation from *salsal┼л╠Бkam.

Griffith

Root up the race of Raksasas, O Indra rend it in front and crush it in the middle.
How long hast thou bebaved as one who wavers? Cast thy hot dart at him who hates devotion:

English translation:

тАЬRegulator (of the world, provide us) with horses for our welfare, and when you are seated near to us may we become mighty, enjoying abundant food, and ample riches, and may there be to us wealth accompanied by progeny.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

It is for our well-being and with your prize-seeking (horses), o leader, that you will sit down to many great refreshments.
Might we be winners of lofty wealth. Let your portion, conferring
offspring, be in us, Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

It is difficult to know how to construe the first p─Бda of this vs. I take it as a nominal main clause expressing the purpose of the subordinate clause in b. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) as a parallel subordinate clause with p─Бda b, for which a verb (ausziehst тАШset out forтАЩ) must be supplied – all dependent on p─Бda c. Renou as part of a single subord. cl.

introduced by y├бd in b, also all dependent on c. Each of these solutions has drawbacks. Mine requires nothing to be supplied (RenouтАЩs supplies less than GeldnerтАЩs), and it also avoids two problems produced by RenouтАЩs interpr: a worrisomely late position of y├бd and an untethered ca in the middle of p─Бda a. But mine comes with a certain awkwardness of expression and an ill-assorted conjoined pair (тАЬfor well-being and with horsesтАЭ).

However the various interpr. of ab differ, they all agree in taking ─Бs├бtsi as the verb in the subor. cl. introduced by y├бd, thus showing the older non-imperatival (that is, subjunctive) value of the so-called тАЬ-si imperative.тАЭ

English translation:

тАЬBring to us, Indra, splendid affluence; we rely on the bounty of you who are fond of giving; our desire is as insatiable as the fire of the ocean; appease it, lord of infinite riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Bring hither to us a brilliant portion, Indra. Might we deposit it amid the surplus of your giving.
As if in the (sea-)basin, desire spreads out in us. Fulfill it, goods-lord of goods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Grassmann analyses dh─лmahi as passive, but this is rightly rejected by all standard tr.: the numerous other examples of this form are all transitive. What then should we supply as object? I take the line of least resistance, importing bh├бgam from the preceding p─Бda. I take the b p─Бda to mean that we hope to take the portion Indra brings us now and put it together with the superfluity of his previous gifts (and those to come) (deс╣гс╣З├бsya тАж prarek├й). Geldner (sim. Witzel Got┼Н) does not construe these two nouns together, but takes deс╣гс╣З├бsya as a partitive genitive, supplying the obj. of dh─лmahi (тАЬWir m├╢chten von deiner Gabe etwas auf Vorrat zur├╝cklegenтАЭ), while Renou takes the verb as reflexive: тАЬpuissions nous nous placer тАжтАЭ The Pp. and all standard analyses take ┼лrv├б as underlying nom. ┼лrv├бс╕е; I, however, take it as loc. ┼лrv├й. Though Geldner and Renou tr. the word as тАШseaтАЩ, it really refers to the container, in this case the sea-basin, and so logically what stretches out is not the container itself but the liquid in the container. (Witzel Got┼Н tr. Beh├дlter, but keep it as nom.)

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGratify this our desire (of wealth) with cows, with horses, with shining treasure, and make us renowned; the wise Ku┼Ыikas, desirous of heaven, offer praise to you Indra, with pious (prayers).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Invigorate this desire with cows, with horses, with recompense in gold, and you will (further) spread it out.
Seeking the sun, the inspired poets, the Ku┼Ыikas, have made with their thoughts a (ritual) conveyance for you, for Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The conjoined verbs in ab, manday─Б тАж papr├бtha┼Ы ca, are in different moods, imperative and subjunctive respectively. Or so it seems: in the sandhi context manday─Б g├│bhiс╕е the apparent impv. manday─Б could represent subjunctive *manday─Бs.

However, I donтАЩt think this is necessary; impv. and subj. are both future-oriented moods, and in fact in this passage the pairing functions as a sort of covert conditional: тАЬ(if) you invigorate it, it will spread.тАЭ K├╝mmel (321), fld by Witzel Got┼Н, construes candr├бvat─Б r─Б╠Бdhas─Б with the 2nd verb, but both the accent on papr├бthaс╕е and the position of the ca make it clear that papr├бthaс╕е must begin a new clause.

Griffith

With kine and horses satisfy this longing with very splendid bounty skill extend it.
Seeking the light, with hymns to thee, O Indra, Kusikas have brought their gift, the singers.

Geldner

Dieses Verlangen stille mit Rindern, mit Rossen, mit blinkender Ehrengabe und dehn es noch aus ! Nach dem Sonnenlicht verlangend haben die beredten Kusika┬┤s mit Gedichten dir, dem Indra, ein Fahrzeug bereitet.

Grassmann

Befried’ge diesen Wunsch durch Ross und Rinder, und mach ihn weit durch gl├дnzende Geschenke; Nach Gl├╝ck verlangend brachten mit Gebeten dem Indra Gaben Ku├зiker, die S├дnger.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, lord of cattle, (divide the clouds and send us) rain, whence nutritious food may come to us; showerer (of benefits), you are spread through the sky, and powerful through truth; Maghavan, consider yourself as our protector.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Keep breaking open the cowpens for us, (break out) the cows, lord of cows; let winnings and victory-prizes together come to us.
You are the ruler of heaven, you bull, whose blusterings are real. For us, bounteous one, become a giver of cows.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Schaeffer (136) sees no particular repetitive function in the well-attested intensive d├бrdar-; she considers it simply lexicalized. Therefore my тАЬkeep breaking openтАЭ may impose a semantic nuance that does not belong to this stem. However, at the very least it takes pl. objects here (gotr─Б╠Б, g─Б╠Бс╕е), so it could be considered тАЬobjektsdistributivтАЭ (for which term see Schaeffer 86-87).

Griffith

Lord of the kine, burst the kine’s stable open: cows shall be ours, and strength that wins the booty.
Hero, whose might is true, thy home is heaven: to us, O Maghavan, grant gifts of cattle.

Geldner

Schlag uns Rinderherden heraus, du Rinderbesitzer ! F├╝r uns sollen sich die Gewinne, die Belohnungen ansammeln. Du bist der Himmelsherr, o Bulle, dessen Eifer echt ist. Sei uns fein ein Rinderschenker, du Gabenreicher!

Grassmann

Erschliess die St├дll’ und Rinder, Herr der Rinder, uns m├╢gen kommen Gaben und Gen├╝sse; Im Himmel wohnest, wahrhaft starker Held du, o Reicher, sei uns reichlich K├╝he spendend.

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреЛ (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) рдЗрд╕ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдо рдореЗрдВ рдХрд┐ (рднрд░реЗ) рдЬрд┐рд╕рдореЗрдВ рдзрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддреЗ рдФрд░ (рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛рддреМ) рдзрди рдЖрджрд┐ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ (рд╢реБрдирдореН) рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рд╕реЗ рд╡реГрджреНрдз (рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдореН) рдмрд╣реБрдд рдзрди рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдиреГрддрдордореН) рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрдд рд╣реА рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрддреНрддрдо (рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдореН) рд╕рдореНрдкреВрд░реНрдг рдЕрд░реНрдереА рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдореБрджреНрджрдИ рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд░реНрдереА рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдореБрджреНрджрд╛рд▓реЗ рдХреЗ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдп рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рд╡рдЪрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╢реНрд░реЛрддрд╛ (рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдореН) рддреЗрдЬрдГрд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рдХреЛ (рд╕рдорддреНрд╕реБ) рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐) рдШреЗрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА рдореЗрдШреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреА рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЗ (рдШреНрдирдиреНрддрдореН) рдирд╛рд╢рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛ рдФрд░ (рдзрдирд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдорд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рд╕рдВрдЬрд┐рддрдореН) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдЬреАрддрдиреЗ рд╡рд╛ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН) рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХреА рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рд╣реБрд╡реЗрдо) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ рдЙрд╕рдХрд╛ рдЖрдкрд▓реЛрдЧ рднреА (рдКрддрдпреЗ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдЖрд╣реНрд╡рд╛рди рдХрд░реЗрдВ реереиреирее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ рд╢рд░реАрд░ рдФрд░ рдЖрддреНрдордмрд▓ рд╕реЗ рдмрдврд╝реЗ рдЕрд╕рдВрдЦреНрдп рдзрди рдХреЗ рджреЗрдиреЗ рдФрд░ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЗ рдЬреАрддрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдзрд░реНрдорд┐рд╖реНрда рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рдореЗрдВ рдирдореНрд░рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡ рдФрд░ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рддреАрд╡реНрд░рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡ рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдкрд╛рд▓рдирдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА рдХреЛ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдКрдкрд░ рдирд┐рдпрдд рдХрд░рдХреЗ рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рд╕реБрдЦ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реВрдЬрд┐рдпреЗ реереиреирее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХреЗ рдХреГрддреНрдп рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣реЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рддреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдЪреМрдерд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдпрдорд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рднрд░реЗ рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛рддреМ рд╢реБрдирдВ рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдВ рдиреГрддрдордВ рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдореБрдЧреНрд░рдВ рд╕рдорддреНрд╕реБ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдШреНрдирдиреНрддрдВ рдзрдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрдЬрд┐рддрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╣реБрд╡реЗрдо рддрдВ рдпреВрдпрдореВрддрдп рдЖрд╣реНрд╡рдпрдд реереиреирее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╢реБрдирдореН) рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╡реГрджреНрдзрдореН (рд╣реБрд╡реЗрдо) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕реЗрдо (рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдореН) рдмрд╣реБрдзрдирд╡рдиреНрддрдореН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН) рджрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдореН (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) (рднрд░реЗ) рдмрд┐рднреНрд░рддрд┐ рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдВрд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН (рдиреГрддрдордореН) рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рдиреГрд╖реВрддреНрддрдордореН (рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛рддреМ) рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╛рдиреНрдзрдирд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдиреН рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреН рд╕рдирдиреНрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рднрдЬрдиреНрддрд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдВрд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗред рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╛рд╕рд╛рддрд╛рд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдордирд╛режред рдирд┐рдШрдВреж реиред резренред [(рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдореН) рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдирд╛рд░реНрдердорд░реНрдерд┐рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд░реНрдерд┐рд╡рдЪрдирд╢реНрд░реЛрддрд╛рд░рдореН] (рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдореН) рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рдореН (рдКрддрдпреЗ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдп (рд╕рдорддреНрд╕реБ) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ (рдШреНрдирдиреНрддрдореН) рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдиреНрддрдореН (рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐) рдЖрд╡рд░рдХрд╛ рдШрдирд╛ рдЗрд╡ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╕реИрдиреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ (рд╕рдВрдЬрд┐рддрдореН) рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧреНрдЬрдпрд╢реАрд▓рдореН (рдзрдирд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рд╢реНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдореН реереиреирее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдпреВрдпрдВ рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рддреНрдордмрд▓рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрджреНрдзрдорд╕рдЩреНрдЦреНрдпрдзрдирдкреНрд░рджрдВ рдирд░реЛрддреНрддрдордВ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рдЬреЗрддрд╛рд░рдВ рдзрд░реНрдорд┐рд╖реНрдареЗ рд╕рд╛рдзреБрдВ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯреЗрд╖реНрд╡рддреНрдпреБрдЧреНрд░рдВ рдкрд╛рд▓рдХрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдирдВ рд╕реНрд╡реЛрдкрд░рд┐ рдорддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рддрддрдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдпрддреЗрддрд┐ реереиреирее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрдХреГрддреНрдпрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ
